<div id="review_484186970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484186970" />
    <a title="Deborah Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/954028-deborah-markus"><img alt="Deborah Markus" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/484186970?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Markus" href="/user/show/954028-deborah-markus">Deborah Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954028-deborah-markus?shelf=good-gift-idea">good-gift-idea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954028-deborah-markus?shelf=christmas-prezzie">christmas-prezzie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954028-deborah-markus?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer484186970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13218031432955541065">Things from this book I actually heard while working at a bookstore:<br/><br/><i>"Where's your true fiction section?"</i><br/><br/>(To this day I have no idea what the person meant.)<br/><br/><i>"You must get so much time to read, just sitting here surrounded by books."</i><br/><br/>(I once had a customer assume I'd read everything in the store. It was a relatively small bookstore rather than one of the big chains, but still -- not cool to be indignant that I haven't read <i>every</i> title we stock.)<br/><br/><i>"I'm looking for a book for my son. He's only seven but</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13218031432955541065" style="display:none">Things from this book I actually heard while working at a bookstore:<br /><br /><i>"Where's your true fiction section?"</i><br /><br />(To this day I have no idea what the person meant.)<br /><br /><i>"You must get so much time to read, just sitting here surrounded by books."</i><br /><br />(I once had a customer assume I'd read everything in the store. It was a relatively small bookstore rather than one of the big chains, but still -- not cool to be indignant that I haven't read <i>every</i> title we stock.)<br /><br /><i>"I'm looking for a book for my son. He's only seven but he's so advanced; it's like he has the brain of a twenty-year-old. What would you recommend?"</i> <br /><br />(Proud parents and grandparents always come in looking for books for a child of a certain age -- but said child is, of course, so gifted that he needs something much more intellectual than the idiotic stuff kids his age usually read. Ugh. Don't get me started on the woman who insisted her eight-year-old granddaughter only ever read Shakespeare. I wanted to ask what this little girl thought of the scene where Othello thinks his wife is cheating on him, so he starts talking to her as if he's her pimp.)<br /><br /><i>Bookseller: Could you put that cigarette out, please?<br />Man: Why?</i><br /><br />(The guy I called out on this one didn't actually question me, and he had the good grace to look sheepish. But he also clearly thought nobody would notice he was smoking <i>in a bloody bookstore</i> if he held his cigarette very discreetly. Apparently bookstore clerks have no sense of smell. But that's okay, because it's not as if we're surrounded by merchandise that's practically begging to catch on fire. Good thing paper doesn't absorb odors, and bookcovers are only <i>improved</i> by the occasional sprinkle of ash!)<br /><br />Things from this book I <i>wish</i> I'd heard while working at a bookstore:<br /><br /><i>"Did Beatrix Potter ever write a book about dinosaurs?"<br /><br />"I've got a while before my bus. Are you and any of the other customers interested in playing cards?"<br /><br />Parent speaking to a misbehaving child: "There should be no yelling unless someone is on fire!"<br />Child: "What if a weasel is robbing the store?"</i><br /><br /><br />You don't have to have worked at a bookstore to love this book. But you do need to love books. And you have to blush if you're one of the people who's ever walked into a bookstore looking for a particular book -- but you don't remember the title, or the author, or exactly what the book's about. But you think it might have a blue cover. (This has come up for every bookseller and librarian I've ever met.)<br /><br />Oh, and I'd like to take this opportunity to give a shout-out to the woman who got mad at me because she couldn't remember the title of the book she wanted <i>or</i> the author's last name, but she <i>did</i> know the author's <i>first</i> name, and why couldn't we alphabetize our books <i>that</i> way for a change? </span>
  <a data-text-id="13218031432955541065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7701602196056252988">What kind of people do you find in a bookstore? Smart people? Intellectuals? Old ladies? People looking for a bathroom?<br/>Time changes and with time, people. For me, libraries and bookstores are sanctuaries. Great places to breath, talk and recommend books. But I'd never in my life had thought it would be a a place to crack up with weird people and their weird questions.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>CUSTOMER: Hi, I just wanted to ask: did Anne Frank ever write a sequel?</i>
</b><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407283668ra/10668395.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>CUSTOMER: Yeah, but Voldemort killed Cedric, who’s </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText7701602196056252988" style="display:none">What kind of people do you find in a bookstore? Smart people? Intellectuals? Old ladies? People looking for a bathroom?<br>Time changes and with time, people. For me, libraries and bookstores are sanctuaries. Great places to breath, talk and recommend books. But I'd never in my life had thought it would be a a place to crack up with weird people and their weird questions.<br><br><b>
  <i>CUSTOMER: Hi, I just wanted to ask: did Anne Frank ever write a sequel?</i>
</b><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407283668ra/10668395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>CUSTOMER: Yeah, but Voldemort killed Cedric, who’s played by Robert Pattinson, and now Voldemort’s playing Edward’s role in Wuthering Heights, because Edward’s character is Heathcliff. I think that Emily Bronte’s trying to say something about vampires.<br></i>
</b> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419537822ra/13089518.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Until this book, working in a bookstore was my idea of volunteer work. Honestly, would you call it a job? Now I suspect those folks deserve more than just a <i>thank you</i> after leaving the bookstore, they deserve a hug. And a raise. <br><br>Because what kind of people do you find in a bookstore but weirdos like us?</span>

<div id="review_512692771" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512692771" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2569035-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455213348p2/2569035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512692771?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/2569035-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2569035-mark?shelf=comic-work">comic-work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2569035-mark?shelf=books-for-the-smallest-room">books-for-the-smallest-room</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512692771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10018816800009746405">From time to time I get emails through that purport to be saying lovely or cute or witty things that children/students/Lawyers/policeman/dogs/raw vegetables etc etc are supposed to have said or written in different situations. They are regularly funny and clever and i enjoy reading them but I as equally regularly read them with a heavy pinch of salt. For every genuinely funny thing that is recorded there are oodles that I cannot believe were ever really said. They are created, made up. This in i</span>
  <span id="freeText10018816800009746405" style="display:none">From time to time I get emails through that purport to be saying lovely or cute or witty things that children/students/Lawyers/policeman/dogs/raw vegetables etc etc are supposed to have said or written in different situations. They are regularly funny and clever and i enjoy reading them but I as equally regularly read them with a heavy pinch of salt. For every genuinely funny thing that is recorded there are oodles that I cannot believe were ever really said. They are created, made up. This in itself does not take away the fun of reading them but it does dampen my enthusiasm a little because it is treating me like a gullible fool or idiot.<br /><br />This book struck me in much the same way. It is a collection of comments and conversations 'gathered' by booksellers and put into this short book which is perfect for dipping into and smiling over but the vast majority of the entrys have never been said seriously. I do not care what the publishers may claim, I do not believe they are real. Not because people do not say stupid things, I myself do quite often, but because that is the vast majority of these comments. <br /><br />More often then not, they are being offered to us not as witty and amusing and clever things people have said but just feeding us an opportunity to laugh at people rather than with. To belittle the stupid or the 'ill-educated'. <br /><br />In small doses it was amusing but if i read it for too long i found myself getting annoyed, not at the inanity of the contributors but at the arrogant superciliousness of the author. <br /><br />An example of the disingenuousness of the book is on the back cover.<br /><br />'Do you have this children's book i've heard about? It's supposed to be very good. It's called "Lionel Ritchie and the Wardrobe"<br /><br />Now I am sorry but nobody ever said that; No they didn't Ms Campbell. That is a clever little joke but nobody ever really said it unless it was heavily tongue in cheek. Your book does not allow for tongue-in-cheek, your book is dismissive and sneery.<br /><br />There are examples after examples of this and it does tend to annoy after a while. Buy this book, stick it in your loo and read it over the course of months rather than a day or so. That way you will laugh at the wit, smile at the imagination of Ms Campbell and not be so annoyed that she has been a tad dishonest in presenting this as reality. Some, maybe a good many, are genuine but loads of them just did not ring true. People are often stupid but not as stupid as she tries to portray. <br /><br />Thinking about it further, it smacked a little of some of those antiquarian bookshops one goes into and because you are wearing shorts, sandals and a t shirt they look dismissively down their nose and assume you are looking for some 'naff little paperback' they could not possibly be holding on their intellectual shelves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10018816800009746405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer339196385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5720990718527685926">Customer: Do you have a true crime section?<br/>Bookseller: Yes (takes customer to section)<br/><br/><i>a few minutes later customer moves to the front door with a book in his pocket</i><br/><br/>Bookseller: Are you going to pay for that book?<br/>Customer: No<br/>Bookseller: (takes book from customers pocket) Please don't come back<br/>Customer: Does this mean I have to bring back all of the other books I've taken?<br/>Bookseller:...<br/><br/>Customer: Do you sell mobile phone top up cards?<br/>Bookseller: No, we're a bookshop, we only sell books<br/>Customer: Not </span>
  <span id="freeText5720990718527685926" style="display:none">Customer: Do you have a true crime section?<br />Bookseller: Yes (takes customer to section)<br /><br /><i>a few minutes later customer moves to the front door with a book in his pocket</i><br /><br />Bookseller: Are you going to pay for that book?<br />Customer: No<br />Bookseller: (takes book from customers pocket) Please don't come back<br />Customer: Does this mean I have to bring back all of the other books I've taken?<br />Bookseller:...<br /><br />Customer: Do you sell mobile phone top up cards?<br />Bookseller: No, we're a bookshop, we only sell books<br />Customer: Not even Telstra?<br />Bookseller: No<br />Customer: How about Vodafone?<br />Bookseller: Erm..No<br />Customer: Do you have any international calling cards then?<br />Bookseller: Well that's not a book and we only sell books, try the newsagent next door.<br />Customer: Oh, isn't this the newsagent?<br />Bookseller: No, we're a secondhand bookshop<br /><br /><br /><br />Customer: Can I use your internet?<br /><br /><br />Customer: Can you photocopy this for me?<br /><br /><br />Customer: I'm looking for a book, it won the Nobel Peace prize for literature. I can't remember it's name but it's a true story.<br /><br /><br />50 year old female customer: Do you have The Hunger Games?<br />Bookseller: It's in our children's section<br />Customer: Will I enjoy it?<br />Bookseller:.....<br /><br />Yes, yes, I was the bookseller in these and many, many more situations just like it. I've had to touch suspiciously wet books that have been removed from peoples underwear (very gross by the way,) I've marvelled at the way people assume we are a babysitting service or that the shop is a playground for their children, my eyes have rolled as I've smiled good naturedly at racists, bigots, religious zealots, care in the community cases and many, many thieves and morons.<br /><br />As Jen Campbell states in her acknowledgements, it was nice to know that these things happen in other bookshops, that people are just plain weird all over the world. <br /><br />A very funny collection of real life experiences that I highly recommend for anyone who has ever thought about working in a bookshop. I know I'm going to have to buy quite a few copies as ideal gifts for my fellow book dealers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5720990718527685926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1662402492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662402492" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8984100-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542163729p2/8984100.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662402492?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/8984100-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662402492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2429424713672982436">It's so good finding out I'm not alone in dealing with weird customers.<br/>I used to work at a stationery store and had a couple of weird customers but not too many.<br/>I also worked at a shoe store that had it's fair share of strange customers but for some reason, the customers that come into a bookstore are on another level. A lot are downright rude, many I don't understand how they function and some I assume have to be pulling my leg, they are that ridiculous.<br/><br/>Here's some of the weird customers I expe</span>
  <span id="freeText2429424713672982436" style="display:none">It's so good finding out I'm not alone in dealing with weird customers.<br />I used to work at a stationery store and had a couple of weird customers but not too many.<br />I also worked at a shoe store that had it's fair share of strange customers but for some reason, the customers that come into a bookstore are on another level. A lot are downright rude, many I don't understand how they function and some I assume have to be pulling my leg, they are that ridiculous.<br /><br />Here's some of the weird customers I experienced just as I was reading this book (I assure you, there's been many more.)<br /><br />1. Customer: *angrily* Kids books these days! <br />Me:... ?<br />Customer: They all have to have morals! *storms out* <br />Me to other bookseller working: We should have a kids section without morals. Wait, that sounds weird.<br /><br />2. Customer: Do you have any other Angelina Ballerina books beside this one? It's been squashed. Me: *goes to inspect book, as children's books generally do get damaged quite easily. Book is in perfect condition, no signs of "squashedness"* We do have some other Angelina Ballerina books, I'll show you where they are. *takes customer to other Angelina Ballerina books*<br />Customer: Oh, but this is your only copy of this one? <br />Me: Yes, sorry, that's our only copy. <br />Customer: Well it's for a gift so I might go look at (other bookstore) because they will hopefully not have squashed books. <br />Me: Sure.<br />*customer stays in store a while and accidentally knocks a hardback picture book onto the ground before hurriedly leaving.*<br />Customer: *comes back into bookstore, picks up an entirely different book to purchase- The Magic Faraway Tree.* Do you think this will be alright for a 4 year old? <br />Me: If it's for bedtime stories that someone will be reading to them, then yes, definitely. <br />Customer: Well obviously. They're not going to read it on their own.<br /><br />23.6.16- <br />Me to customer walking in store: Good morning, how are you?<br />Customer: Good thanks. *walks around a bit*<br />Me: *thinks customer is browsing so continue on with inventory maintenance*<br />Customer: *waits by counter, not asking any questions, just looking at bookmarks, occasionally picking something up*<br />Customer: *starts staring at me intensely* <br />Me: ....Hi, can I help you?<br />Customer: You had an edition of the Jungle Book that's the same as this Alice in Wonderland book, where is it?<br />Me: *looks at Alice in Wonderland book* We have a beautiful Just So Stories that is similar to this edition, would you like me to grab it?<br />Customer: No, it was the Jungle Book. It was here last week.<br />Me: Well we have a whole Jungle Book display in the window, if you have a look you might spot the one you're after. <br />Customer: Okay. *walks out of store* *keeps walking, never to return again* <br /><br />19.7.16- <br />Customer: Do you have 'Miss Pedigree's Home for Wayward Children?<br /><br />26.7.16- <br />Me to customer walking in: Hi how are you?<br />Customer: *glares* walks off to shelves.<br />*5 minutes later*<br />Customer: *rudely* When are you getting new books in?<br />Me: ...sorry?<br />Customer: I'm looking for a particular book. <br />Me: Sure, what's it called, we might be able to order it in for you.<br />Customer: *gives title of book which was originally published in 1985 and is the third in an unknown series*<br />Me: We'd be able to order it in for you, but it's highly unlikely that we'll receive a book that was published in 1985 and is the third in a series in our next delivery...<br />Customer: Okay then I'll order it. *eyeroll*<br /><br />27.7.16-<br />*phone rings*<br />Me: Robinsons Bookshop Eastland this is Grace speaking.<br />Customer: Hi, I'm looking for a book that I saw in your store but I can't remember what it's called. It was about a coffee shop or a bakery or something.<br />Me: Was it 'The Little Coffee Shop of Kabul'?<br />Customer: No... it wasn't that one...<br />Me: Do you remember what it looks like or whereabouts in the store that you saw it?<br />Customer: I don't remember what it looks like but when you go into Highpoint they have a sales table and it was on the bookshelves near that.<br />Me: ...you saw it at the Highpoint store, not our store?<br />Customer: Yeah. I think the authors name must begin with one of the early letters in the alphabet. <br />Me: Is it Jenny Colgan's 'The Loveliest Chocolate Shop In Paris'? Highpoint definitely have that in stock.<br />Customer: Hmmm... I dunno. I'll have to go in again.<br /><br />19/8/16-<br />Customer: *looking through a brand new Lift-The-Flap book, lifting flaps as she goes.*<br />Customer: Do you have any other copies of this one? This one's a bit used.<br /><br />24/8/16-<br />*phone rings*<br />Me: [Bookshop name], Grace speaking.<br />Customer: Hi would you be able to look up a book for me?<br />Me: Sure thing, what's it called?<br />Customer: Alice In Wonderland<br />Me: *is assuming someone is pulling me leg* uhhh... there's many editions of Alice in Wonderland, is there a particular one you are after?<br />Customer: A children's edition.<br />Me:.... there are quite a few children's editions, did you have one in mind?<br />Customer: I'm just on your website now [website shows what we have in stock so the customers can more easily make decisions]. <br />Me: Oh good, if you have the ISBN I can look up which one you are after. <br />Customer: *gives ISBN*<br />Me: *types in ISBN. 0 in stock.* So it seems we don't have that edition at the moment but our [other] store does. I can get it transferred here if you like. <br />Customer: *rudely* I need it by tomorrow.<br />Me: Okay sure.<br />Customer: Can you recommend one for a 6 year old?<br />Me: *looks at our Alice selection, picks up an Usborne Illustrated edition* Yep, I've got one here. *after many attempts manages to give customer ISBN so she can see it*<br />Customer: Oh that one looks good. Who's the author?<br />Me:...it's still Lewis Carroll... <br />Customer: Okay I'll get my husband to pick it up today.<br /><br />13.1.17- <br />Customer: There was a Sherlock Holmes book at your store in the city. It was green. Do you have it?<br />Me: This is where we keep all of our Sir Arthur Conan Doyle books, is it one of these?<br />*it's not, I call the city store to see if they have it. They don't.*<br />Customer: it was actually written by Sherlock Holmes, it was his stories. It was $49. <br />Me:.... Sorry, it looks like we don't have it. <br /><br />13.1.17 (it's Friday the 13th, all the nutters are out.)<br />Customer: Do you have a men's section?<br />Me: ...uhhhh *??????*<br />Customer: Like a section on men's stories. <br />Me: Well, we have a biography section, a sports section, a personal development section....<br />Customer: Yeah, that last one sounds good.<br />Me: Okay, follow me.<br /><br />18.1.17<br />*customer complains about phones not working, despite us only opening ten minutes ago*<br />Customer (abruptly): Graffiti Moon.<br />Me: Would you like me to see if we have that in stock?<br />Customer: Well that's what I'm here for, to buy a book. *guffaws* <br />*we don't have it, customer storms out.*<br /><br />19.1.17<br />Customer: Hi, I'm just wondering if you can tell me if you have any Michael Scott. I don't understand how you arrange things here. *waves hands about, gesturing madly at the shelves that are categorised and arranged alphabetically by author, like almost every bookshop in existence*<br />Me: Was there a particular book you were after?<br />Customer: I just want to know if you have any Michael Scott. <br />Me: Sure, we stock him in Kids Fiction under 'S' for Scott. Would you like me to show you?<br />Customer: In Kids Fiction or Children's Fiction? <br />Me: Let me show you. *takes customer there.*<br />*later*<br />Customer: You didn't have his third book there. That's what we were after.<br />Me: Oh, that's why I asked if there was a particular book that you were after. Do you want me to see if we can get it in for you?<br />Customer: No. <br /><br />19.1.17<br />Customer: Maybe you can help me, I'm looking for an author...Pablo.... Oh.... what's his name... Pablo.... You know who I mean though?<br />Me: *thinks I do, but can't be sure* ...uuuuh<br />Customer: He wrote The Alchemist.<br />Me: Paulo Coehlo?<br />Customer: Yes! I was just saying it the Italian way. <br /><br />23.1.17-<br />Customer approaches counter: Your hair is nice. I like the colour. <br />Me: Thanks!<br />Customer: It matches your dress well. <br />Me: Thanks...<br />Customer: It's not very good for now though. <br />Me: ....uhhh?<br />Customer: It's more of a winter colour. <br />Me:...okay.<br />Customer: I didn't mean to insult you.<br />Me: ....sure....<br /><br />1/2/17<br />Really glad that 'customer' liked my review/shelf talker of "The Girl in 6E" enough to shoplift it....<br />*update*<br />....and it's sequel.<br /><br />2/2/17<br />(let me just tell you, this week has been horrendous but this one is a funny one that I deal with 30 times a day.)<br />*putting through a sale for a customer*<br />Me: If your card has a chip in it, insert it in the top.<br />Customer: *goes to swipe, I can see card has a chip. The Eftpos machine will not allow chip cards to swipe.*<br />Me: So just insert the chip in the top there *points*<br />Me: Now select account by pushing 1,2 or 3 on the screen *which displays what account corresponds to what number*<br />Customer: How do I do that?<br />Me:... by pushing 1,2 or 3. <br />(This one might be funny only to me, but it's because I have to tell people sometimes up to three times to insert the chip in their card. "Just insert the chip in the top there *customer swipes or moves machine around searching for paywave*... so that one has a chip, you'll need to insert it in the top *goes to insert chip in the bottom where there is nothing to insert into*.... Just insert the chip in the top" *points exactly where, customer usually inserts it the wrong way*.... leaving me to eventually grab the card and insert it myself.)<br /><br />7/2/17<br />Customer: Do you have Chaos and Calm? *pronounces 'calm' like 'can' despite sounding very Australian, I had to ask her to repeat it.<br />Me: I'll just check our stock.<br />Customer: Is this different to Angus &amp; Robertson?<br />Me: Yes, we are a different shop.<br />Customer: Oh, you probably won't have the book then.<br />Me: Why is that?<br />Customer: *slightly taken aback at my sass* ....because... they had it online...<br />Me: Well, we currently don't have it because we have sold out. Would you like me to order you a copy?<br />Customer: That's okay, I'll order it online.<br />Me: Sure.<br /><br />8/2/17<br />Customer: Do you have Bitten By An Elephant?<br />Me: No, sorry, it's currently only available online or from the Law Institute Bookshop.<br />Customer: Readings have it.<br />Me: Well, they must have gotten it directly from the author or publishing company, as it doesn't currently have a major supplier.<br />Customer: So you can order it, you just choose not to.<br />Me: No... I can't order it as they do not have a major supplier.<br />Customer: So you don't sell any self-published books?<br />Me: We do, but the authors have to apply directly to our head office to commission their book. <br />Customer: Well, I'll just go to Readings then. <br />Me: Uh huh.<br /><br />15/2/17-<br />Customer: I need something to tide me over until the next Robin Hobb book comes out.<br />Me: Sure, I'll take you over to the Fantasy section. Have you read any Brandon Sanderson?<br />Customer: Nope.<br />Me: Well, the Mistborn series is really popular, I've read the first book and the world-building is spectacular in the first half and then the second half is really fast-paced plot-driven. There's also Name of the Wind by Patrick Rothfuss which is beautifully written, amazing setting and characters and is one of the most popular fantasy books we sell. Otherwise we have the Lightbringer series by Brent Weeks which has a really cool magic system and is very popular, the fourth book has just come out. We also have the Dark Tower series by Stephen King which is his magnum opus, it's very much a western fantasy but it's absolutely amazing. We also have Nevernight which is written by an Australian author and is about an assassin in Venice. <br />Customer: *seriously* You're not a fantasy reader, are you?<br />Me: ....? I've read Mistborn, Name of the Wind, The Dark Tower series, Game of Thrones, the Way of Shadows, a number of Terry Pratchett's-<br />Customer: Yeah, you probably don't realise but Terry Pratchett was really anti-religious. Most people get really mad when they realise.<br />Me: Uh huh... <br />Customer: I'm a bit worried about the new Robin Hobb. It's called the Assassin's End (*side note* no, it's called the Assassin's Fate*) so obviously she kills off the main character. <br />Me:....*basically given up on the conversation and just nodding along complacently*<br />Customer: I'll just get the first Mistborn book. <br />(First customer of the day and I have not had enough coffee to deal with self-righteous, smug customers.)<br /><br />22/2/17 (phone call)<br />Customer: Hi, I was looking at ordering some Joy Dettman books through you.<br />Me: Sure thing, which ones were you after.<br />Customer: *lists books*<br />Me: Sure, I can get those in for you.<br />Customer: How much will they be?<br />Me: They are $19.99 each.<br />Customer: Oh that's no good, I want the $30 ones.<br />Me: I'm sorry... they're priced at $19.99. <br />Customer: Why is that?<br />Me: It's because they are older titles. They're smaller than the new release books.<br />Customer: Oh but I want the bigger ones. The $30 ones.<br />Me: I'm sorry, but once they are about a year old they get printed in the smaller format. <br />Customer: Well what ones come in the large one?<br />Me: At the moment only 'Silent Inheritance' because it just came out last year. <br />Customer: Well that's no good, I already have that one. So what $30 books can you get?<br />Me: Of Joy Dettman's?<br />Customer: Yes! That's what I'm asking you!!<br />Me:.... as I said... just 'Silent Inheritance'. The others are all the $19.99 smaller formats. <br />Customer: Well I guess I'm stuck with them. Yes, order them in.<br /><br />22/3/17-<br />Customer: I'm looking for a book on wildflowers.<br />Me: Hmm... okay let me take you to the gardening section, but it is quite small so I'm not sure if we have anything.<br />Customer: Well it's not the type of book that is kept in gardening.<br />Me:.... well I'm not sure where else we would keep them.<br /><br />LET ME JUST TAKE YOU TO THE "WILDFLOWER" SECTION THEN!!!<br /><br />(This one is an old one but it's good.)<br />Customer: *lifts "Seriously Funny- Terry Pratchett" off of the counter and turns to a page.* Give a man a fire and he's warm for a day, but set fire to him and he's warm for the rest of his life. *customer laughs heartedly*<br />Me: Yes- his short, short life.<br />Customer:.... Oh... I just got it. Because he dies.<br /><br />30/3/17- <br />*customer calls first thing in the morning*<br />Customer: I'm looking for Pete the Cat books. <br />Me: It looks like we have one single copy and one of our stores has the Storybook Collection which has 7 books for $19.99<br />Customer: How much is it?<br />Me: $19.99<br />Customer: For each book?<br />Me: No, it's $19.99 for the whole collection. For 7 books. <br />Customer: Oh that's so cheap! Why is it so cheap?<br />Me: I'm not sure, I guess because they're kids books. They're not usually that expensive. <br />*spend 5 minutes going over all the stories contained in the collection*<br />Customer: So you can get it from the other store for me?<br />Me: Yes, we can do that it should be here tomorrow and we can let you know as soon as it's arrived.<br />Customer: *silence*<br />Me: ... Would you like me to get it in for you?<br />Customer: That's okay, I'll just get it online.<br />Me: ...okay.<br /><br />31/3/17- <br />*An elderly lady walks in*<br />Customer: Hi, I've ordered a book and I just wanted to see whether it was in yet. It's 'Immortal Unchained.'<br />Me: Sure, I'll just have a look and see when we're expecting that one. *looks it up, pub date was 3 days ago, supplier still has no stock. I call the supplier to figure out what's going on, to no avail.* <br />So the supplier is going to call me back once they have a confirmed date and then I'll pass that information along to you.<br />Customer: Have you ever read this series?<br />Me: No, I haven't. Is it good?<br />Customer: Yes, it's not your typical vampire novel. The vampires faint after having sex. <br />Me: oh.... well I suppose some people cry and some people faint. <br />Customer: Very true! You should read it.<br />Me: ....okay.<br /><br />7/4/17-<br />*I call a customer to book them into an event*<br />Me: Hi this is Grace calling from the bookshop, you wanted to book in for the Sam Wood 28 event?<br />Customer: Hi yes, I've tried calling you all morning and I couldn't get on to you.<br />Me: Yes, we just opened at 10, which is when we open every day. <br />Customer: Oh okay... I'd like to book in for 3 people.<br />Me: Sure thing, I'll put the booking under your name.<br />Customer: Now is your store outside? <br />Me: Yes, we are in the outside section with all the restaurants.<br />Customer: So where will the event be held?<br />Me: Next door in the enclosed Atrium.<br />Customer: So what happens if it rains?<br />Me: ... the Atrium is inside.<br />Customer: I thought you said you were outside?<br />Me:... yes, we are in the outside section of the shopping centre. Our store and the atrium has a roof though, we are just not inside the shopping centre. <br />Customer: Are you near Jimmy Grants?<br />Me: Yes, we are in that section.<br />Customer: If I stand at Jimmy Grants will I be able to see you?<br />Me: The entrance to the shopping centre is in the way but if you just walk around it we'll be right there.<br />Customer: Okay.... so you're in the outside bit though.<br />Me: ...YES.<br />Customer: And how long is the workout?<br />Me: *thinking about the book titled 28: Change your life in 28 minutes.* It's 28 minutes long. <br />Customer: Okay... and the book signing is at 1... and that will go for how long? <br />Me: I'm not sure, probably half an hour? It's directly after the workout though. <br />Customer: Okay so booked in for 3 people at the workout in the outdoor section. <br />Me: Yes, but it has a roof. <br />Customer: Okay, thanks.<br /><br />7/4/17 (they're all out on a Friday)<br />Customer: Hi, do you have Donna Leon's Body of Evidence? I've had a look and can't find it.<br />Me: *looks it up* Doctored evidence by Donna Leon?<br />Customer: No, Body of Evidence.<br />Me: Well, we don't have either of those at the moment.<br />Customer: I called this morning and you did.<br />Me: ....I've been here by myself all morning and nobody called about that, are you sure it was our shop?<br />Customer: No actually it was on your website.<br />Me: *our store is called Robinsons* ... did you perhaps get it confused with Angus &amp; Robertson's website?<br />Customer: Definitely not. If you don't have it, don't worry. *storms out*<br /><br />7/4/17 (omg this is getting ridiculous now, it's only 12 o'clock)<br />Customer: Do you have any offer?<br />Me: *is standing directly in front of a giant '25% off SALE' sign.* *points to sign*<br />Customer: Oh 25% off! Where are your pop up books? <br />Me: *takes them down to the section. Customer pulls out pop up book for $29.99*<br />Customer: So how much is that? <br />Me: It's 25% off of $29.99<br />Customer: and what does that equal?<br />Me: *in my head, eff you for making me math* Well 10% is about $3 so about $7.50.<br />Customer: It's $7.50?? <br />Me: No, it's $7.50 off of $29.99 so it's about $22.50.<br />Customer: Oh. *puts book back in shelf, spine facing in.* *I grab it before he can ruin entire display*<br /><br />7/4/17-<br />Customer: Do you have a men's section?<br />Me: No...<br /><br />12/4/17-<br />*customer calls*<br />Customer: Do you have any Lego Nexus Knights books?<br />Me: Yes, we do, we have a few, is there any you are after?<br />Customer: No it's okay I'll come in. <br />*customer arrives, asks about books, I show her*<br />Customer: We need Level 2 reader Nexus Knights junior fiction and you don't have any. We got ready and came all this way for nothing. That's why I called.<br />Me: .... we can order level 2 readers in for you, it was why I asked if there was anything specific. <br />*eyeroll*<br />~continued in comments!~</span>
  <a data-text-id="2429424713672982436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UhYgzbVLT5gXZgeM1Q8/ThlQgCNbolVKSLoMTaYgtVedvJJLqBC0N9sIQJz/Hxd96EmVlmgmf9BVnTZfORXyzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D+VEp0pYF6HZFoY6KYF8yHzJSCJe/qyZweNZ5HzPYu7AT/YhVwPsDhV4wSoDkVT7jdBdl216hgPcxGP24/oldA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

مضيفيها، تُعمق الكاتبة فهمها للعمليات الفكرية ورؤية العالم المتجسدة في اللغة وتعبيرها المكتوب. هذا العمل هو استكشاف حساس للذات والطبيعة أشبه بجوهرة صغيرة من النثر الشعري. \n\nإلينيد جراميش / وُلدت في (ذاكرة السمكة الذهبية) للكاتبة والممثلة السويسرية مونيك شـﭬيتر عن دار نشر بارثيان في أبريل 2015. تعمل الآن على روايتها الأولى. فاز كتابها (المرأة التي تجلب المطر) بجائزة الكتابة الويلزية الجديدة 2015، id=\"freeTextContainer8502417268129978255\">•	«يستحق «فالادا» ثناءً عاليًا لكتابته عن الحياة بهذه الواقعية، وهذا الصدق، وهذا القرب» - «هرمان هسه»\n•	«يمكن اعتبار «فالادا» بطلًا، كاتبًا بطلًا بقي على قيد الحياة الوقت الكافي فقط لرد الضربة على ظالميه» - «ألان فورست»\n\nبصراحة مُؤثِّرة ومُبهرة قلَّ <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8502417268129978255\" style=\"display:none\">•	«يستحق «فالادا» ثناءً عاليًا لكتابته عن الحياة بهذه الواقعية، وهذا الصدق، وهذا القرب» - «هرمان هسه»\n•	«يمكن اعتبار «فالادا» بطلًا، كاتبًا بطلًا بقي على قيد الحياة الوقت الكافي فقط لرد الضربة على ظالميه» - «ألان فورست»\n\nبصراحة مُؤثِّرة ومُبهرة قلَّ نظيرها في الأدب العالمي، يخبرنا «هانز فالادا» عن السلوك القهري لمدمن المورفين، إذ عرف من خبرته الخاصة نشوة لحظة التعاطي والكارثة التي تليها.\nتعود كتابة «تقرير موضوعي عن سعادة مدمن المورفين» إلى ثلاثينيات القرن العشرين، إلا أن النَّص لم يُنشر قبل نهاية التسعينيات.\nأما النَّص الثاني في هذه المجموعة، والذي كُتب في الفترة نفسها، «ثلاث سنوات لم أكن إنسانًا»، فيتناول تجربة السجن، وهو أيضًا مُستوحى من حياة المؤلف.\nينجح «فالادا»، على الرغم من أسلوبه الموضوعي الجاف الذي يندرج في تيار «الموضوعية الجديدة»، أو ربما بفضل هذا الأسلوب، في صياغة نصَّين آسرين، شيِّقين، وقويَّين في صدقهما، وسُخريتهما، وفرادتهما في تاريخ الأدب الحديث.\nنُقدِّم القصتين هنا كأول أعمال «فالادا» بالعربية، وقد ترجمهما عن الألمانية سمير جريس ببراعة غنية عن التوصيف.\n\n•	«كل شيء في حياتي ينتهي في كتاب» - «هانس فالادا»\n\n«هانس فالادا» (1893-1947)، واسمه الحقيقي «رودولف ديتسن»، من أشهر الكُتاب الألمان في القرن العشرين. بأسلوبه الموضوعي الجاف الذي يندرج في تيار «الموضوعية الجديدة» كتبَ عددًا من الروايات الاجتماعية الكبيرة التي حققت نجاحًا باهرًا، مثل رواية «ماذا بعد، أيها الرجل الصغير؟» (1932)، التي عالج فيها الانحدار الاجتماعي الذي شهده موظف بسيط خلال الأزمة الاقتصادية التي اجتاحت العالم في عشرينيات القرن الماضي. حققت هذه الرواية نجاحًا عالميًّا، تكرر في أعماله اللاحقة مثل «ذئب بين ذئاب» (1937) و«كلٌّ يموت من أجل نفسه فحسب» (1947).\nلم تفقد أعمال «فالادا» راهنيتها وأهميتها حتى اليوم، فما زالت تصدر في طبعات جديدة، وما زالت تُترجم وتُعاد ترجمتها إلى عديد من لغات العالم، كما تحول عدد كبير من أعماله إلى أفلام سينمائية وأعمال مسرحية.\nقضى «فالادا» فترات من حياته في مصحات العلاج من إدمان المورفين، كما وقع فريسة إدمان الخمر، ولذلك كان الإدمان موضوعًا مسيطِرًا على بعض أعماله التي صدرت بعد وفاته، مثل رواية «السكير» (كتبها عام 1944 وصدرت للمرة الأولى عام 1950) ومجموعة «تقرير موضوعي عن سعادة مدمن المورفين» التي صدرت لأول مرة عام 1997، ومنها اخترنا قصتَي هذا الكتاب، اللتين تترجمان إلى العربية للمرة الأولى.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8502417268129978255\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13161436903919687033">​Jen Campbell is a bestselling author and award-winning poet. Her short story collection The Beginning of the World in the Middle of the Night is published by Two Roads, her children's picture books, Franklin's Flying Bookshop, Franklin and Luna go to the Moon, and Franklin and Luna and the Book of Fairy Tales are published by Thames & Hudson. Her poetry collection The Girl Aquarium is published b</span>
  <span id="freeText13161436903919687033" style="display:none">​Jen Campbell is a bestselling author and award-winning poet. Her short story collection The Beginning of the World in the Middle of the Night is published by Two Roads, her children's picture books, Franklin's Flying Bookshop, Franklin and Luna go to the Moon, and Franklin and Luna and the Book of Fairy Tales are published by Thames &amp; Hudson. Her poetry collection The Girl Aquarium is published by Bloodaxe.<br /><br />Jen is also the author of the Sunday Times bestselling Weird Things Customers Say in Bookshops series, and The Bookshop Book. Her poetry pamphlet The Hungry Ghost Festival is published by The Rialto. She's a recipient of an Eric Gregory Award and won the Jane Martin Poetry Prize. <br /><br />Jen worked as a bookseller for ten years and now has a Youtube channel, where she talks about all things books. She also runs a podcast called BOOKS WITH JEN, is Vlogger in Residence for the Poetry Book Society, offers writing workshops and editorial services, and runs a book club for TOAST. <br /><br />She grew up in the north east of England and now lives in London. She is represented by Charlie Campbell at Kingsford Campbell. </span>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_16174631'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16174631-more-weird-things-customers-say-in-bookshops?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">More Weird Things Customers Say in Bookshops<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/5211857.Jen_Campbell?origin=series_works\">Jen Campbell<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.78 avg rating &mdash; 6,391 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2013\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer15192693069813897151\">Customer (holding up a book): What’s this? The Secret Garden? Well, it’s not so secret now, is it, since they bloody well wrote a book about it!\n\nWeird Things Customers Say in Bookshops was a Sunday Times bestseller, and could be found displayed on b<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText15192693069813897151\" style=\"display:none\">Customer (holding up a book): What’s this? The Secret Garden? Well, it’s not so secret now, is it, since they bloody well wrote a book about it!\n\nWeird Things Customers Say in Bookshops was a Sunday Times bestseller, and could be found displayed on bookshop counters up and down the country. The response to the book from booksellers all over the world has been one of heartfelt agreement: it would appear that customers are saying bizarre things all over the place - from asking for books with photographs of Jesus in them, to hunting for the best horse owner’s manual that has a detailed chapter on unicorns. \n\nCustomer: I had such a crush on Captain Hook when I was younger. Do you think this means I have unresolved issues?\n\nMore Weird Things Customers Say in Bookshops has yet more tales from the antiquarian bookshop where Jen Campbell works, and includes a selection of ‘Weird Things...’ sent in from other booksellers across the world. The book is illustrated by the BAFTA winning Brothers McLeod.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"15192693069813897151\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n She really dies at the end – that’s why the diary finishes. She was taken to a concentration camp.<br />CUSTOMER: Oh... that’s terrible.<br />BOOKSELLER: Yes, it was awful -<br />CUSTOMER: I mean, it’s such a shame, you know?
